The Magnet Analogy: God's Protection of Prophethood
Maturidi presents the first part of his answer using a magnet analogy.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Maturidi uses the analogy of the magnet stone to explain that God prevents those with unique powers from falsely claiming prophethood.

Core Idea
God gives unique powers but also blocks their misuse for false prophecy.

In this lesson, we examine Maturidi's first response to the fourth objection. The objector claimed a prophet's miracles might come from a special natural power. Maturidi counters with a striking analogy: if God grants someone a unique power, He also prevents them from using it to claim prophethood falsely, just as a magnet stone is prevented from having other properties. This sets the stage for a deeper argument about the Quran's uniqueness.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once and its translation. Notice the concise logical structure. The analogy may seem unusual but is central to Maturidi's argument.
2
Understand the magnet analogy
Identify how the magnet stone’s property (attracting iron) is used to illustrate the principle of divine prevention. Why might God grant a power but also prevent its misapplication?
Consider the uniqueness of the magnet: it only attracts iron, not other things.
3
Connect to prophethood
Maturidi states that if God knows a person might falsely claim prophethood using a special power, He would not give that power. Reflect on how this resolves the objection.
This shows that miracles are not reducible to natural talents.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وجواب الرابع أن الله تعالى إذا خص أحدا بقوة لا يشاركه فيها أحد يمنعه عن دعوى النبوة باللفظ كما منع من يظفر بحجر المغناطيس، ولو علم أنه يدعى لا يعطيه. والثاني أن لا أحد في شيء له فضل قوة إلا طمع غيره استتمام ذلك أو عمل ذلك النوع بقدر قوته، والدليل ما يخرج من الطباع وبعد، فإنه لو كان له في ذلك فضل قوة بها عمل لكان لا يتمكن نيلها، وليست لهم؛ إذ لا يوجد مثل ذا في شيء من الأمور، دل أن الله جعل فيه ليكون آية لقوله بهم وسنذكر جمل هذه التأويلات بعد الفراغ من فصوله وقوله على البديهة، فقد أمهلوا، مع ما لم يحتمل أن يكون من البشر يعلم بفضل القوة ما تسأل عنه، وقد ما لم تكلفوا الإشعار ثم نصب الحروب وجمع الأعوان وبذل الأعيان ثم اقتتال الأقران والمبادرات الفظيعة، فلو كان ومهم يحتمل القيام بذلك أيسر عليهم، ثم قد دعوا إلى اتيان السورة، نحو ثلاث آيات، لو احتملها وسع البشر لكان ساعة من النهار كافية لذلك
And the answer to the fourth [objection] is that God, exalted, if He distinguishes someone with a strength in which no one shares with him, He prevents him from claiming prophethood by [mere] words, just as He prevented the one who obtains the magnet stone. And if He knew that he would claim [prophethood], He would not give it to him. And the second [point] is that no one has excellence of strength in anything without another coveting the completion of that or performing that type [of act] according to his own strength. The evidence [is] what emerges from natures and afterwards. For if he had in that an excellence of strength by which he acted, then attaining it would not be possible, and it is not for them, since there is no like of this in any of the matters. This indicates that God placed it in him to be a sign for His statement. And we will mention the summary of these interpretations after finishing its sections and His statement upon intuition. They were given respite, along with what it is not possible that a human knows by virtue of strength what you ask about, and they were not tasked with [producing] poetry, then waging wars, gathering supporters, sacrificing lives, then fighting peers and terrible initiations. For if it were possible for them to undertake that, it would be easier for them. Then they were called to produce a sura, about three verses, if it were within human capacity, an hour of the day would suffice for that.
Source pages p. 792

Commentary
This passage is an answer to the fourth objection against prophethood. The objector likely argued that a prophet's miracles could be due to some special natural power or talent, and therefore not divine. Maturidi responds in two parts. First, he explains that if God gave someone a unique power, He would also prevent that person from claiming prophethood unless it were truly from Him, just as He prevents the magnet stone from having any other property. Second, he argues that no one has such a unique power in any field without others coveting and attempting to imitate that power. The fact that the Arabs, despite their great love for eloquence and life itself, could not produce anything like the Quran—even a short sura—proves that the Quran is beyond human capacity and is a divine sign. Maturidi also notes that the Arabs were challenged to produce similar poetry or prose, but they failed, indicating that the Quran's inimitability is not due to any special strength but to its divine origin.

Key Terms
قوة خاصة
دعوى النبوة
حجر المغناطيس

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What does the magnet analogy illustrate in Maturidi's first argument?
A) That magnets are a special creation of God.
B) That if God gives a unique power, He also prevents its false use.
C) That the magnet stone has many properties.
D) That prophets use natural powers.

Key Takeaway
Maturidi uses the magnet stone analogy to show that God controls the use of unique powers, ensuring they cannot be exploited to falsely claim prophethood.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever harbored the ambition to gain recognition or authority in religious matters, even in a small way? How does this passage's logic—that God prevents false claimants from succeeding—expose the futility and danger of such ambition? What must you do today to uproot it from your heart?
?
When you see someone with an extraordinary talent or spiritual gift, do you automatically assume it is a sign of divine favor? Based on this lesson, what should you examine before drawing such a conclusion, and how might you have been deceived before?
?
If God, in His foreknowledge, would not give a unique power to someone who would misuse it, then what does your own possession of abilities say about His trust in you? Are you using them in a way that honors that trust, or are you at risk of proving yourself unworthy of the gifts He has given?

The Inimitability of the Quran as Divine Proof
Maturidi presents the second argument: the inability to imitate the Quran as evidence of divine origin.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Maturidi uses the failure of the Arabs to imitate the Quran as evidence that it is beyond human capacity and a divine sign.

Core Idea
The Arabs' inability to produce a sura like the Quran proves it is from God.

In this second part of his answer, Maturidi presents a powerful argument based on the Quran's inimitability. He observes that no one has a unique power in any domain without others aspiring to match it. The Arabs, despite their eloquence and willingness to sacrifice, could not produce even a short sura similar to the Quran. This failure, along with the historical challenge, demonstrates that the Quran is not the product of human strength but a divine miracle.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify the main claim
Read the Arabic and translation. Maturidi states a general principle: no one has excellence of strength without others coveting and attempting to imitate it. Then he applies this to the Quran.
2
Understand the evidence from nature
Maturidi says 'the evidence is what emerges from natures'. Reflect on how human nature drives people to imitate excellence. If the Quran were from human power, others would have succeeded in imitation.
3
Trace the historical challenge
Notice the description of the Arabs' willingness to wage wars and sacrifice lives to oppose Islam, yet they failed to produce a sura. This shows the Quran's unique nature.
The challenge to produce even three verses is mentioned at the end.

?

?

?
Maturidi says that the Arabs' failure proves God placed the inimitability in the Quran as a sign. That sign is meant to remove all doubt. If you have doubts about prophethood, will you honestly examine this argument, or will you turn away like those who chose war over truth?

Ibn al-Rawandi's Dichotomy and the Quran's Inimitability
Maturidi presents Ibn al-Rawandi's argument and the first Quranic proof of inimitability.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Ibn al-Rawandi's argument about the necessity of tawatur and how Maturidi counters with the Quran's inimitability as the first proof.

Core Idea
The Quran's unique composition proves prophethood because the Arabs failed to imitate it despite their ability and motivation.

Imam Maturidi begins by reporting Ibn al-Rawandi's challenge: either all historical reports are unreliable, or mass-transmitted reports (tawatur) are accepted, which would include prophetic reports. Maturidi then announces his intention to refute this using four Quranic proofs. The first proof is the Quran's linguistic inimitability: though composed in the Arabs' own style, they could not produce anything like it when challenged, despite their eloquence and love for life.

Guided Path
1
Ibn al-Rawandi's Dilemma
Read the opening where Ibn al-Rawandi presents two possibilities for establishing knowledge of the past. Notice how he tries to force a choice between complete skepticism and accepting tawatur.
He wants to show that accepting tawatur leads to accepting prophetic reports.
2
Maturidi's Response Framework
See how Maturidi states he will refute the objection using four aspects from the Quran. This sets up the structure.
3
The First Proof: Inimitability
Read the first proof carefully. Maturidi argues that the Quran's composition, though within Arab linguistic norms, was inimitable. Despite being challenged, the Arabs could not produce similar verses, proving divine origin.
This shows their incapacity was not due to lack of motivation but due to the Quran's miraculous nature.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أقاويل ابن الروندى في الرسالة وبيان فسادها قال الشيخ رحمه الله: احتج ابن الراوندي بما تقدم من الأغذية والسموم في إثبات الرسالة، ثم قال: لا يخلو الأمر في الخبر إما أن لا يثبت البتة، فيجب الجهل بالأيام الماضية والأماكن النائية والوقائع السالفة، أو نقبل التواتر وما يضطر إليها فوجب به أخبار الرسل، ولا قوة إلا بالله. ثم نذكر جمل ما يبين فساد طعنه من وجوه الحجج بالقرآن؛ إذ هي من وجوه: أحدها بنظمه من غير أن كان فيه غريب مبتدع يخرج ذلك عن عرف العرب، بل هو بأعذب لفظ وأملح نظم، وقد احتملت العرب المؤن التي هلكوا فيها، ولا يحتمل ترك الأمر اليسير مع التحدي والتقريع، مع سلامة أحب الأشياء إليهم وهي الحياة وتبدل المهج مع ضنهم بها إلا عن عجز ظهر لهم من أنفسهم طباعا أو امتحانا. والثاني بيان جميع الأمور التي بها علم العلماء أهل الكتاب مع العلم بمن شهد رسول الله أنه لم يك اختلف إليهم، ولا كان يخط كتابا بيمينه فيحتمل استعادته، ثبت أن ذلك كان بتعليم الله إياه. والثالث الإخبار بما يكون له من الفتوح، ودخول الخلق في دينه أفواجا وإظهار دينه على الأديان في وقت ضعفه وقلة أعوانه وكثرة أعدائه، فكان على ما أخبره القرآن، وبالله التوفيق. في القرآن أصول جميع النوازل التي تكون إلى القيامة، دل أنه عالم الغيب حتى أعلمه أصول ذلك. والرابع أن الله تعالى جمع وأيضا ما أظهر من موافقة القرآن سائر كتب الله، وبيان نعت محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم وأمته كقوله: الذي يجدونه مكتوبا عندهم، وقوله: محمد رسول الله، وقوله: يعرفونه كما يعرفون أبناءهم، من غير اجتراء أحد منهم على إنكار ذلك ودفعه، ثبت أن الذي أنزل هذه الكتب هو الله سبحانه فجعلها كلها متفقة: على اختلاف الأزمنة وتباعد الأوقات؛ ليعلموا أن القرآن من عند من جاء منه الكتب، وأن الذي جاء منه الكتب قديم لم يزل حجته في الأولين والآخرين واحدا.
The sayings of Ibn al-Rawandi in the letter and the demonstration of their corruption. The Shaykh (may God have mercy on him) said: Ibn al-Rawandi argued using what was previously mentioned about foods and poisons for establishing prophethood. Then he said: The matter regarding report (khabar) is free from either that it is not established at all, so ignorance of past days, remote places, and previous events would be necessary, or we accept tawatur (mass transmission) and what compels [assent] thereby, so the reports of the messengers are necessary. And there is no power except by God. Then we will mention the summary of what shows the corruption of his objection among the aspects of proofs from the Qur'an. For they are among the aspects: One of them is its composition, without there being in it any strange or novel [expression] that takes it out of the custom of the Arabs; rather it is in the sweetest wording and most graceful composition. The Arabs bore hardships in which they perished, but they could not bear abandoning the easy matter despite the challenge and reproof, with the safety of the most beloved things to them, namely life, and the exchange of lives despite their stinginess with them, except due to an incapacity that appeared to them from themselves by nature or trial. The second [is] the exposition of all the matters by which the scholars of the People of the Book learned, along with the knowledge that those who witnessed the Messenger of God [knew] that he did not go to them, nor did he write a book with his right hand, so that it could be possible that he copied it. It is established that this was by God's teaching. The third [is] the informing of what would be for him of conquests, the entry of people into his religion in multitudes, and the manifestation of his religion over [other] religions at a time of his weakness, few supporters, and many enemies. It was as the Qur'an informed. With God is success. In the Qur'an are the principles of all events that will occur until the Day of Resurrection. This indicates that He is the Knower of the Unseen, to the extent that He informed him of the principles of that. The fourth [is] that God, exalted, gathered — and also what was manifest of the agreement of the Qur'an with the rest of God's books, and the description of Muhammad (peace be upon him) and his community, such as His saying: 'Whom they find written with them,' and His saying: 'Muhammad is the Messenger of God,' and His saying: 'They recognize him as they recognize their sons,' without anyone among them daring to deny or repel that. It is established that the One who sent down these books is God, exalted, so He made them all agreed, despite differences of times and distances of periods, so that they might know that the Qur'an is from the One from whom the [other] books came, and that the One from whom the books came is eternal, His proof is one in the first and the last.
Source pages p. 792

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of Ibn al-Rawandi's argument regarding the transmission of prophetic reports. Maturidi first cites Ibn al-Rawandi's claim: either reports are not reliable at all (leading to ignorance of history), or we accept tawatur (mass transmission) which necessitates accepting the reports of the messengers. Maturidi then presents four Quranic proofs to show the corruption of Ibn al-Rawandi's objection. The first proof is the Quran's inimitability (i'jaz): its style is within Arab custom yet beyond human capacity, as the Arabs failed to produce anything like it despite being challenged and despite their love for eloquence. The second proof is that the Prophet (peace be upon him) was unlettered; he did not learn from the People of the Book, so the knowledge in the Quran must be from God. The third proof is the Quran's prophecies of future events (like conquests and the spread of Islam), which came true. The fourth proof is the agreement of the Quran with previous scriptures and the descriptions of the Prophet found in them, without any of the People of the Book being able to deny it. This proves that the Quran is from God and that God's proof is one and eternal.

Key Terms
التواتر
التحدي
الإعجاز

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Quran's inimitability is subjective and based on taste.
Correction: Maturidi shows it is objective: the Arabs were motivated and capable in other compositions but could not produce anything like the Quran, proving their incapacity was real.

Checkpoint
According to Ibn al-Rawandi, what are the two possibilities for establishing knowledge of the past?
A) Skepticism or tawatur
B) Reason or revelation
C) Induction or deduction
D) Memory or testimony

Key Takeaway
Ibn al-Rawandi's argument forces a choice between skepticism and tawatur, but Maturidi counters by demonstrating the Quran's miraculous nature as divine proof.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You call yourself a Muslim, yet do you truly live as if the Quran is the inimitable word of God? When it challenges you to change, do you respond with the same stubbornness as the Arabs who could not produce a verse like it? What verse has confronted you recently, and have you obeyed it or dismissed it?
?
The Arabs loved life more than anything, but the Quran was so compelling that their failure revealed an incapacity you also share. When was the last time the Quran's words pinned you against a wall, leaving you no excuse? Did you submit, or did you run to distractions?
?
You now know that the Arabs' failure was not due to inability but to divine protection of the miracle. Does this truth shatter your pride? Have you ever felt that your own resistance to the Quran is a form of incapacity – not intellectual, but of the heart? What will you do today to let the Quran overwhelm you?

Prophethood
beginner
3 min
Second Proof: The Prophet's Illiteracy and Divine Teaching
Maturidi presents the second proof: the Prophet's illiteracy and his knowledge of previous scriptures.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Prophet's illiteracy and the accurate knowledge in the Quran about previous scriptures serve as a proof of prophethood.

Core Idea
The unlettered Prophet could not have copied scriptures, so his knowledge must be from God.

The second Quranic proof that Maturidi presents focuses on the Prophet's illiteracy. The People of the Book recognized in the Quran matters of their own scriptures, yet they knew the Prophet never studied with them nor could he write. This proves that the Quran was taught to him directly by God.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Proof's Structure
Read the passage and note how Maturidi establishes two facts: the scholars of the People of the Book learned correct matters, and the Prophet was illiterate.
The conjunction 'with' (مع) links the two points.
2
Understand the Implication
Because the Prophet did not go to them nor write anything, he could not have copied from them. The only source is divine teaching.
This refutes any claim that the Prophet learned from earlier sources.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أقاويل ابن الروندى في الرسالة وبيان فسادها قال الشيخ رحمه الله: احتج ابن الراوندي بما تقدم من الأغذية والسموم في إثبات الرسالة، ثم قال: لا يخلو الأمر في الخبر إما أن لا يثبت البتة، فيجب الجهل بالأيام الماضية والأماكن النائية والوقائع السالفة، أو نقبل التواتر وما يضطر إليها فوجب به أخبار الرسل، ولا قوة إلا بالله. ثم نذكر جمل ما يبين فساد طعنه من وجوه الحجج بالقرآن؛ إذ هي من وجوه: أحدها بنظمه من غير أن كان فيه غريب مبتدع يخرج ذلك عن عرف العرب، بل هو بأعذب لفظ وأملح نظم، وقد احتملت العرب المؤن التي هلكوا فيها، ولا يحتمل ترك الأمر اليسير مع التحدي والتقريع، مع سلامة أحب الأشياء إليهم وهي الحياة وتبدل المهج مع ضنهم بها إلا عن عجز ظهر لهم من أنفسهم طباعا أو امتحانا. والثاني بيان جميع الأمور التي بها علم العلماء أهل الكتاب مع العلم بمن شهد رسول الله أنه لم يك اختلف إليهم، ولا كان يخط كتابا بيمينه فيحتمل استعادته، ثبت أن ذلك كان بتعليم الله إياه. والثالث الإخبار بما يكون له من الفتوح، ودخول الخلق في دينه أفواجا وإظهار دينه على الأديان في وقت ضعفه وقلة أعوانه وكثرة أعدائه، فكان على ما أخبره القرآن، وبالله التوفيق. في القرآن أصول جميع النوازل التي تكون إلى القيامة، دل أنه عالم الغيب حتى أعلمه أصول ذلك. والرابع أن الله تعالى جمع وأيضا ما أظهر من موافقة القرآن سائر كتب الله، وبيان نعت محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم وأمته كقوله: الذي يجدونه مكتوبا عندهم، وقوله: محمد رسول الله، وقوله: يعرفونه كما يعرفون أبناءهم، من غير اجتراء أحد منهم على إنكار ذلك ودفعه، ثبت أن الذي أنزل هذه الكتب هو الله سبحانه فجعلها كلها متفقة: على اختلاف الأزمنة وتباعد الأوقات؛ ليعلموا أن القرآن من عند من جاء منه الكتب، وأن الذي جاء منه الكتب قديم لم يزل حجته في الأولين والآخرين واحدا.

What two facts does Maturidi use in the second proof?

Key Takeaway
The second proof shows that the Quran's accurate knowledge of previous scriptures, combined with the Prophet's illiteracy, confirms divine origin.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If the Prophet ﷺ, who was unlettered, brought knowledge that only God could give, what is your excuse for not taking the Quran as the ultimate authority in your life? Will you today commit to reading its verses as if they were directly from Allah to you?
?
You claim to believe that the Quran is from God, yet how often do you treat it as just another book? Reflect on a specific area of your life where you have ignored its guidance. What will you change starting today?
?
The scholars of the People of the Book had studied scriptures for years, yet the Prophet ﷺ surpassed them without any human teacher. Do you truly humble yourself before this miracle, or do you secretly feel that your own knowledge is sufficient? Ask Allah to make you reliant on His teaching alone.

Prophethood
intermediate

Third Proof: Prophecies of Future Events
Maturidi presents the third proof: the Quran's prophecies of future events and its comprehensive principles.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Quran's accurate prophecies of future conquests and the spread of Islam prove that it is from the Knower of the Unseen.

Core Idea
The Quran's foretelling of future victories and the inclusion of all future events' principles show it is from God.

The third proof relies on the Quran's predictive power. At a time when the Prophet was weak and outnumbered, the Quran foretold conquests and the spread of Islam, which later happened exactly as stated. Moreover, the Quran contains principles for all future events, indicating it came from the All-Knowing.

Guided Path
1
Read the Prophecy
Notice the specific predictions: conquests, people entering Islam in multitudes, and the religion prevailing over others.
These were made when Muslims were few and weak.
2
Reflect on the Fulfillment
The fact that they came true proves the Quran is from God, who knows the unseen.
Maturidi also adds that the Quran contains the principles (أصول) of all events until the Day of Resurrection.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

What does Maturidi say is in the Quran regarding future events?
A) Detailed accounts of every event
B) The principles of all events until the Day of Resurrection

D) A promise of worldly success for all believers

Key Takeaway
The Quran's accurate prophecies and universal principles confirm it is from the Knower of the Unseen, proving prophethood.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If the Quran contains the principles of all events until the Day of Resurrection, what does that mean for how you approach the trials and decisions in your life? Will you commit to seeking those principles in the Quran before relying on your own planning?
?
The Quran predicted victory at a time of extreme weakness. What 'weakness' in your own faith or life do you doubt God can turn into victory? Will you trust His promise today as the early Muslims did?
?
The Quran's prophecies came true exactly as stated. How does this certainty about the past affect your certainty about the future promises of the Quran, like the Day of Judgment? Is your belief about the Hereafter as firm as your belief about these fulfilled historical prophecies? What needs to change?

Fourth Proof: Agreement with Previous Scriptures
Maturidi presents the fourth proof: the agreement of the Quran with previous scriptures and the recognition of the Prophet.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the agreement of the Quran with earlier scriptures and the recognition of the Prophet by the People of the Book serve as the fourth proof of prophethood.

Core Idea
The Quran's consistency with previous books, despite differing times, proves they share the same divine source.

The fourth proof focuses on the harmony between the Quran and earlier scriptures. The Quran describes the Prophet and his community exactly as found in the Torah and Gospel. The People of the Book recognized this but could not deny it. This agreement, despite the time gaps, shows that all scriptures come from one eternal God.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Key Points
Read the passage and note three elements: the agreement of the Quran with previous books, the description of the Prophet in those books, and the inability of the People of the Book to deny it.
Maturidi quotes Quranic verses about the Prophet being found written with them.
2
Understand the Logical Conclusion
Because the Quran agrees with previous books, and those books are from God, the Quran must also be from God. And the fact that the People of the Book could not refute it despite their knowledge confirms the truth.
This refutes the idea that the Prophet fabricated the Quran.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أقاويل ابن الروندى في الرسالة وبيان فسادها قال الشيخ رحمه الله: احتج ابن الراوندي بما تقدم من الأغذية والسموم في إثبات الرسالة، ثم قال: لا يخلو الأمر في الخبر إما أن لا يثبت البتة، فيجب الجهل بالأيام الماضية والأماكن النائية والوقائع السالفة، أو نقبل التواتر وما يضطر إليها فوجب به أخبار الرسل، ولا قوة إلا بالله. ثم نذكر جمل ما يبين فساد طعنه من وجوه الحجج بالقرآن؛ إذ هي من وجوه: أحدها بنظمه من غير أن كان فيه غريب مبتدع يخرج ذلك عن عرف العرب، بل هو بأعذب لفظ وأملح نظم، وقد احتملت العرب المؤن التي هلكوا فيها، ولا يحتمل ترك الأمر اليسير مع التحدي والتقريع، مع سلامة أحب الأشياء إليهم وهي الحياة وتبدل المهج مع ضنهم بها إلا عن عجز ظهر لهم من أنفسهم طباعا أو امتحانا. والثاني بيان جميع الأمور التي بها علم العلماء أهل الكتاب مع العلم بمن شهد رسول الله أنه لم يك اختلف إليهم، ولا كان يخط كتابا بيمينه فيحتمل استعادته، ثبت أن ذلك كان بتعليم الله إياه. والثالث الإخبار بما يكون له من الفتوح، ودخول الخلق في دينه أفواجا وإظهار دينه على الأديان في وقت ضعفه وقلة أعوانه وكثرة أعدائه، فكان على ما أخبره القرآن، وبالله التوفيق. في القرآن أصول جميع النوازل التي تكون إلى القيامة، دل أنه عالم الغيب حتى أعلمه أصول ذلك. والرابع أن الله تعالى جمع وأيضا ما أظهر من موافقة القرآن سائر كتب الله، وبيان نعت محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم وأمته كقوله: الذي يجدونه مكتوبا عندهم، وقوله: محمد رسول الله، وقوله: يعرفونه كما يعرفون أبناءهم، من غير اجتراء أحد منهم على إنكار ذلك ودفعه، ثبت أن الذي أنزل هذه الكتب هو الله سبحانه فجعلها كلها متفقة: على اختلاف الأزمنة وتباعد الأوقات؛ ليعلموا أن القرآن من عند من جاء منه الكتب، وأن الذي جاء منه الكتب قديم لم يزل حجته في الأولين والآخرين واحدا.
The sayings of Ibn al-Rawandi in the letter and the demonstration of their corruption. The Shaykh (may God have mercy on him) said: Ibn al-Rawandi argued using what was previously mentioned about foods and poisons for establishing prophethood. Then he said: The matter regarding report (khabar) is free from either that it is not established at all, so ignorance of past days, remote places, and previous events would be necessary, or we accept tawatur (mass transmission) and what compels [assent] thereby, so the reports of the messengers are necessary. And there is no power except by God. Then we will mention the summary of what shows the corruption of his objection among the aspects of proofs from the Qur'an. For they are among the aspects: One of them is its composition, without there being in it any strange or novel [expression] that takes it out of the custom of the Arabs; rather it is in the sweetest wording and most graceful composition. The Arabs bore hardships in which they perished, but they could not bear abandoning the easy matter despite the challenge and reproof, with the safety of the most beloved things to them, namely life, and the exchange of lives despite their stinginess with them, except due to an incapacity that appeared to them from themselves by nature or trial. The second [is] the exposition of all the matters by which the scholars of the People of the Book learned, along with the knowledge that those who witnessed the Messenger of God [knew] that he did not go to them, nor did he write a book with his right hand, so that it could be possible that he copied it. It is established that this was by God's teaching. The third [is] the informing of what would be for him of conquests, the entry of people into his religion in multitudes, and the manifestation of his religion over [other] religions at a time of his weakness, few supporters, and many enemies. It was as the Qur'an informed. With God is success. In the Qur'an are the principles of all events that will occur until the Day of Resurrection. This indicates that He is the Knower of the Unseen, to the extent that He informed him of the principles of that. The fourth [is] that God, exalted, gathered — and also what was manifest of the agreement of the Qur'an with the rest of God's books, and the description of Muhammad (peace be upon him) and his community, such as His saying: 'Whom they find written with them,' and His saying: 'Muhammad is the Messenger of God,' and His saying: 'They recognize him as they recognize their sons,' without anyone among them daring to deny or repel that. It is established that the One who sent down these books is God, exalted, so He made them all agreed, despite differences of times and distances of periods, so that they might know that the Qur'an is from the One from whom the [other] books came, and that the One from whom the books came is eternal, His proof is one in the first and the last.
Source pages p. 792

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of Ibn al-Rawandi's argument regarding the transmission of prophetic reports. Maturidi first cites Ibn al-Rawandi's claim: either reports are not reliable at all (leading to ignorance of history), or we accept tawatur (mass transmission) which necessitates accepting the reports of the messengers. Maturidi then presents four Quranic proofs to show the corruption of Ibn al-Rawandi's objection. The first proof is the Quran's inimitability (i'jaz): its style is within Arab custom yet beyond human capacity, as the Arabs failed to produce anything like it despite being challenged and despite their love for eloquence. The second proof is that the Prophet (peace be upon him) was unlettered; he did not learn from the People of the Book, so the knowledge in the Quran must be from God. The third proof is the Quran's prophecies of future events (like conquests and the spread of Islam), which came true. The fourth proof is the agreement of the Quran with previous scriptures and the descriptions of the Prophet found in them, without any of the People of the Book being able to deny it. This proves that the Quran is from God and that God's proof is one and eternal.

Key Terms
الكتب السابقة
أهل الكتاب
الموافقة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Quran contradicts previous scriptures and was not known to the People of the Book.
Correction: Maturidi shows that the Quran agrees with earlier scriptures and the People of the Book recognized the Prophet in their texts.

Checkpoint
What is the fourth proof Maturidi presents from the Quran against Ibn al-Rawandi?
A) The Quran's unique composition.
B) The Prophet's illiteracy and lack of learning.
C) The agreement of the Quran with previous scriptures and descriptions of the Prophet.
D) The prophecies of future conquests.

Key Takeaway
The fourth proof shows that the Quran's harmony with previous scriptures, combined with the People of the Book's recognition, confirms it is from the one eternal God.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The People of the Book recognized the truth but some rejected it. Where in your life are you recognizing a truth from Allah but hesitating to act on it? What will you do about it today?
?
The Quran's consistency across time is a sign from the eternal God. Do you treat the Quran as the eternal word that demands your full surrender, or as just another book? What change is needed in your relationship with it?
?
Knowing that God's proof is one throughout history, what is your personal response to the message that has reached you? Are you aligning your life with that unbroken divine call?

The Inimitability of the Quran's Eloquence
Maturidi presents the first proof: the Quran's inimitability.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Arabs' inability to match the Quran's eloquence proves its divine origin.

Core Idea
The Quran's eloquence is beyond human capacity, proven by the Arabs' failure despite extreme motivation.

Maturidi begins his enumeration of proofs by highlighting the Quran's unparalleled eloquence. He argues that the Arabs, despite their mastery of language and willingness to sacrifice everything, could not produce anything similar, demonstrating that the Quran is from Allah.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage about the Quran's composition once without analysis, then read the translation to grasp the argument.
Notice the contrast between the Quran's sweetness and the Arabs' hardships.
2
Identify the logical structure
Maturidi sets up a condition: the Arabs faced a challenge with high stakes (life and death), yet they could not respond. This incapacity proves the Quran's uniqueness.
3
Reflect on the implication
If the Arabs, the most eloquent people, could not produce anything like it, then the Quran must be from Allah.
This is the core of the i'jaz argument.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم نذكر جمل ما يبين فساد طعنه من وجوه الحجج بالقرآن ; إذ هى من وجوه : أخدها بنظمه من غير أن كان فيه غريب مبتدع يخرج ذلك عن عرف العرب ، بل هو بأعذب لفظ وأملح نظم ، وقد احتملت العرب المؤن التي هلكوا فيها ، ولا يحتمل ترك الأمر اليسير مع التحدى والتقريع ، مع سلامة أحب الأشياء إليهم وهى الحياة وتبدل المهج مع ضنهم بها إلا عن عجز ظهر لهم من أنفسهم طباعاً أو امتحانا . والثانى بيان جميع الأمور التي بها علم العلماء أهل الكتاب مع العلم بمن شهد رسول الله أنه لم يك يختلف إليهم ، ولا كان يخط كتابا بيمينه فيحتمل استعادته ، ثبت أن ذلك كان بتعليم الله إياه . والثالث الإخبار بما يكون له من الفتوح ، ودخول الخلق في دينه أفواجا وإظهار دينه على الأديان فى وقت ضعفه وقلة أعوانه وكثرة أعدائه ، فكان على ما أخبره القرآن . والرابع أن الله تعالى جمع في القرآن أصول جميع النوازل التي تكون إلى يوم القيامة ، دل أنه عالم الغيب حتى أعلمه أصول ذلك
Then we mention a summary of what shows the invalidity of his criticism from the aspects of proofs by the Quran; for they are from aspects: First, by its composition, without there being in it any strange or innovated [expression] that takes it out of the custom of the Arabs, rather it is with the sweetest wording and most elegant composition. And the Arabs endured hardships in which they perished, and they would not endure abandoning a trivial matter despite the challenge and reproach, while preserving the dearest of things to them, which is life, and sacrificing lives despite their stinginess with them, except due to an incapacity that appeared to them from themselves naturally or by ordeal. Second: the clarification of all the matters by which the scholars of the People of the Book gained knowledge, along with the knowledge of whom the Messenger of God testified that he did not frequent them, nor did he write a book with his right hand so that it might be possible that he had studied it. It is established that that was by God's teaching him. Third: the informing of what would be his conquests, and the entering of people into his religion in multitudes, and the manifestation of his religion over [other] religions at a time of his weakness, fewness of his helpers, and multitude of his enemies, and it came to pass as the Quran informed him. Fourth: that God, exalted, gathered in the Quran the principles of all events that occur until the Day of Resurrection. It indicates that He is the Knower of the Unseen, so He informed him of the principles of that.
Source pages p. 793

Commentary
This passage is an enumeration of four distinct proofs of prophethood derived from the Quran. Maturidi presents them sequentially. The first proof is the Quran's inimitability: despite the Arabs' renowned eloquence and their willingness to sacrifice everything during the challenge, they could not produce anything like it, proving divine origin. The second proof is that the Prophet, though unlettered and never having studied with the People of the Book, accurately conveyed all the knowledge contained in their scriptures, which must have been taught by God. The third proof is the fulfillment of prophecies regarding future conquests and the triumph of Islam despite initial weakness and opposition, exactly as the Quran stated. The fourth proof is that the Quran contains the principles (أصول) of all events until the Day of Resurrection, demonstrating that its source is the Knower of the Unseen (عالم الغيب), who imparted that knowledge to the Prophet.

Key Terms
إعجاز القرآن
التحدي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the Quran's inimitability is merely about superior literary style.
Correction: Maturidi shows that the argument relies on the Arabs' inability to respond despite the high stakes, proving it is beyond human capability.

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi's first proof, why did the Arabs fail to produce something like the Quran despite the challenge?
A) They did not take the challenge seriously.
B) They lacked the motivation due to peace.
C) Their natural incapacity (عجز) became evident to them.
D) The Quran was revealed in a non-Arabic language.

Key Takeaway
The Quran's unmatched eloquence, coupled with the Arabs' inability to meet the challenge, proves it is from Allah.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

?
The Quran's inimitability is a sign that cuts through human pride. Have you ever let that truth pierce your heart and change the way you live, or do you treat it as an academic fact with no personal weight?

The Unlettered Prophet's Knowledge of Previous Scriptures
Maturidi presents the second proof: the Prophet's knowledge of scripture without learning.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Prophet's accurate knowledge of earlier scriptures, despite being unlettered, proves divine revelation.

Core Idea
The Prophet's unlettered state and accurate scriptural knowledge show his knowledge came from Allah.

The second proof focuses on the Prophet's knowledge of the People of the Book's scriptures. Maturidi argues that since the Prophet was unlettered and never studied with them, his accurate transmission of their knowledge must have been taught by Allah.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation for the second proof. Pay attention to the description of the Prophet's unlettered state.
2
Analyze the logic
The Prophet had full knowledge of the scriptures of the People of the Book, but he never attended their gatherings or wrote anything. The only explanation is that Allah taught him.
This argument relies on the impossibility of acquiring such knowledge naturally.
3
Connect to prophethood
This knowledge is a miracle that confirms his prophethood.

Prophecies of Future Conquests and the Spread of Islam
Maturidi presents the third proof: fulfilled prophecies.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Quran's predictions about future conquests and the triumph of Islam, fulfilled despite initial weakness, prove its divine origin.

Core Idea
The Quran's accurate prophecies about future events, fulfilled exactly, demonstrate it is from Allah.

The third proof draws attention to the Quran's prophecies about conquests and the spread of Islam. Maturidi argues that these predictions came true despite the Prophet's initial weakness and few supporters, which could only be known through divine revelation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation for the third proof. Notice the contrast between the Prophet's weak state and the grand outcomes predicted.
2
Identify the prophecy
The Quran foretold conquests, mass conversions, and the dominance of Islam over other religions.
3
Consider the circumstances
When these prophecies were made, the Prophet was weak, with few supporters and many enemies. Their fulfillment is a powerful proof.
This shows that the knowledge came from the Knower of the Unseen.

The first proof is the Quran's inimitability: despite the Arabs' renowned eloquence and their willingness to sacrifice everything during the challenge, they could not produce anything like it, proving divine origin. The second proof is that the Prophet, though unlettered and never having studied with the People of the Book, accurately conveyed all the knowledge contained in their scriptures, which must have been taught by God. The third proof is the fulfillment of prophecies regarding future conquests and the triumph of Islam despite initial weakness and opposition, exactly as the Quran stated. The fourth proof is that the Quran contains the principles (أصول) of all events until the Day of Resurrection, demonstrating that its source is the Knower of the Unseen (عالم الغيب), who imparted that knowledge to the Prophet.

Key Terms
الفتوح

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) He was strong and had many supporters.
B) He was weak with few helpers and many enemies.
C) He was rich and powerful.
D) The People of the Book supported him.

Key Takeaway
The Quran's fulfilled prophecies about future conquests and Islam's spread, given the Prophet's weak state, prove divine origin.

?

What would change in your daily life if you treated every verse as a concrete, testable truth that has already been verified?
?
If the companions saw these prophecies fulfilled and their faith increased, why does your heart sometimes remain unmoved when you read the same Quran? What is holding you back from having the same certainty they had, and what is one step you can take today to remove that barrier?

By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Quran's inclusion of principles for all future events demonstrates that its source is the All-Knowing.

The Quran's comprehensive principles for all events until Judgment Day show it is from the Knower of the Unseen.

The fourth proof highlights the Quran's comprehensiveness. Maturidi asserts that the Quran contains the principles (أصول) of all events that will occur until the Day of Resurrection. This indicates that its source is Allah, the Knower of the Unseen, who imparted that knowledge to the Prophet.

Second: the clarification of all the matters by which the scholars of the People of the Book gained knowledge, along with the knowledge of whom the Messenger of God testified that he did not frequent them, nor did he write a book with his right hand so that it might be possible that he had studied it. It is established that that was by God's teaching him. Proof from Agreement with Previous Scriptures
Maturidi argues that the Quran's agreement with previous books proves its divine origin.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Maturidi uses the agreement between the Quran and previous scriptures as a proof for the divine origin of the Quran and the prophethood of Muhammad.

Core Idea
The Quran's agreement with earlier scriptures across time points to a single divine author.

Maturidi presents an additional argument for the truth of Islam: the Quran's consistency with previous revealed books. This agreement is not superficial but includes specific descriptions of the Prophet and his followers that the People of the Book could not deny. Let's examine this proof from his Kitab al-Tawhid.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation. Let the author's own logic come through.
Notice the concise style of Maturidi's argument.
2
Identify the key claim
Maturidi states that the Quran agrees with all previous books of God. This is the premise.
3
Observe the evidence provided
He cites three verses that show descriptions of Muhammad and his community found in earlier scriptures. The People of the Book could not deny these.
The absence of denial strengthens the proof.
4
Understand the logical conclusion
Since the books agree despite different times, they must have a single divine source. This source is eternal and His proof remains one.
This conclusion ties directly to the oneness of God.
5
Reflect on the implication
Consider why this argument is persuasive: it uses the internal consistency of revelation as a sign of truth.
This is a common theme in proofs of prophethood.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأيضا ما أظهر من موافقة القرآن سائر كتب الله ، وبيان نعت محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم وأمته كقوله : الَّذِي يَجِدُونَهُ مَكْتُوبًا عِنْدَهُمْ ، وقوله : مُحَمَّدٌ رَسُولُ وقوله : يَعْرِفُونَهُ كَمَا يَعْرِفُونَ أَبْنَاءَهُم، من غير اجتراء أحد منهم على إنكار ذلك ودفعه ، ثبت أن الذى أنزل هذه الكتب هو الله سبحانه فجعلها كلها متفقة : على اختلاف الأزمنة وتباعد الأوقات ؛ ليعلموا أن القرآن من عند من جاء منه الكتب ، وأن الذى جاء منه الكتب قديم لم يزل حجته في الأولين والآخرين واحدا
And also what is shown of the agreement of the Quran with all the books of God, and the description of Muhammad, may God bless him and grant him peace, and his community, as His saying: 'whom they find written with them,' and His saying: 'Muhammad is the Messenger of God,' and His saying: 'they recognize him as they recognize their own sons,' without anyone among them daring to deny or reject that. It is established that the One who sent down these books is God, exalted, so He made them all in agreement, despite the difference of times and distance of periods, so that they know that the Quran is from the One from whom the [other] books came, and that the One from whom the books came is eternal, and His proof remains one for the first and the last.
Source pages p. 793

Commentary
This passage is an additional proof for prophethood based on the agreement between the Quran and previous scriptures. Maturidi points out that the Quran confirms the descriptions of Muhammad and his community found in earlier books (e.g., Torah and Gospel) without any contradiction. The People of the Book themselves could not deny these descriptions. This agreement across different times and contexts demonstrates that all scriptures come from the same divine source—God—who is eternal and whose proof (حجة) remains consistent for all generations.

Maturidi cites three fulfilled predictions as proofs of prophethood.

Learning Objective

Core Idea
Fulfilled predictions prove divine knowledge behind prophethood.

This passage from Maturidi's Kitab al-Tawhid presents several examples of predictions that came true exactly as reported. These events serve as empirical evidence that the Prophet's knowledge was from Allah, confirming his prophethood. Let's examine each proof.

Each prediction came true as foretold, showing that only Allah could have provided that knowledge. This confirms the Prophet's truthfulness.

The Quran's Miracle in the Age of Ignorance
Maturidi describes the jahiliyya context to highlight the Quran's miraculous eloquence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Maturidi uses the historical context of jahiliyya to demonstrate the Quran's miraculous comprehensiveness.

Core Idea
The Quran's proofs are so vast that all human minds together cannot match a tenth.

Maturidi grounds his argument for the Quran's miraculous nature in the historical reality of pre-Islamic Arabia. He points out that the Prophet was sent in an age of profound ignorance and polytheism, yet the Quran emerged with such profound proofs that no combination of scholars could replicate them. This lesson examines that argument and its implications for understanding prophethood and miracles.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Start by reading the Arabic passage and its literal translation carefully. Let the words of Maturidi set the stage for the argument.
Notice the phrase 'ما احتملت بلوغ عشرها' – 'they could not reach a tenth of it.'
2
Identify the key elements
Identify the context (jahiliyya), the claim (the Quran's proofs are inaccessible), and the conclusion (the Quran is miraculous).
Maturidi emphasizes that even the combined effort of all monotheists and scholars falls short.
3
Reflect on the nature of the miracle
Consider that this miracle is not merely literary eloquence but the comprehensiveness and depth of proof that transcends human capacity.
This distinguishes Maturidi's argument from simple claims of literary superiority.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والأصل في هذا أن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم بعث في عصر لم يعرف فيه التوحيد بل كان عباد الأوثان والأصنام والنيران ، فجمع ما أنزل عليه القرآن هو من أنجح ما لو اجتمع موحد و العالم من مضى منهم ومن يكون أبدا على إظهار أدلته ما احتملت بلوغ عشرها ، فضلا عن الإحاطة في ذلك الزمان الذى لا يقدر على موجد واحد ، ولا قوة إلا بالله
And the basis of this is that the Messenger of God, peace be upon him, was sent in an age in which tawheed (monotheism) was not known, rather [people were] worshippers of idols, statues, and fires. So what was revealed to him, the Quran, is from [the category of] that which is most successful: if a monotheist and a scholar from those who have passed and those who will ever be were to gather to manifest its proofs, they would not be able to reach a tenth of it, let alone encompass it, in that age which has no ability for a single existing thing [to comprehend it]. And there is no power except with God.
Source pages p. 794

Commentary
This passage is the underlying principle (الأصل) for the previous proofs. Maturidi emphasizes that the Prophet was sent in a time of deep ignorance (جاهلية) where polytheism prevailed. Despite this, the Quran was revealed with such profound eloquence and proof that even if all monotheists and scholars from past and future were to combine their efforts, they could not produce a tenth of its proofs, let alone fully grasp them. This highlights the Quran's miraculous nature, especially given the context of an age incapable of producing even one such proof. The phrase 'no power except with God' underscores reliance on divine aid.

Key Terms
التوحيد
عباد الأوثان
الأدلة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Quran's miracle is only about its literary eloquence and poetic superiority.
Correction: Maturidi argues that the miracle is about the comprehensiveness of its proofs—so vast that all human minds combined cannot match a tenth of them.

Checkpoint

C) They would need divine inspiration.
D) They could match it if they cooperated.

Key Takeaway
Maturidi establishes that the Quran's miraculous nature lies in its proofs being far beyond any human capacity to produce, even if all scholars cooperated.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

The Quran's Consistency Over Twenty Years
Maturidi argues from gradual revelation to divine origin.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's rational proof that the Quran's internal consistency despite piecemeal revelation indicates it is from Allah, the Knower of the Unseen.

Core Idea
The Quran's seamless unity over twenty years defies human capability.

Maturidi presents a powerful argument for the Quran's divine origin: it was revealed gradually over twenty years, yet its style and content are perfectly consistent. If it were human-authored, contradictions would have crept in. This lesson unpacks that reasoning and shows how it points to Allah alone.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic text and its translation. Notice that Maturidi states a fact (gradual revelation) and draws a conclusion (no variation in nazm and agreement).
The word nazm refers to the Quran's unique literary composition.
2
Identify the argument's structure
Break down the passage into premise, conditional statement, and conclusion. The premise: revelation over 20+ years in parts. The observation: it maintains a single standard. The contrary-to-fact conditional: if from creatures, they would differ. The conclusion: it is from the Knower of the Unseen.
3
Reflect on the key term 'nazm'
Understand that nazm is not just the meaning but the whole compositional style, including word choice, rhythm, and coherence. Maturidi emphasizes this consistency.
This counters a common misunderstanding that only themes are consistent.
4
Apply the argument
Consider: if any human group tried to produce a book of similar length and style over two decades, would it avoid all internal contradictions? This thought experiment makes the proof tangible.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأيضا أن القرآن أنزل في عشرين سنة فصاعدا بالتفاريق ، ما خرج على وزن واحد من النظم ، وعلى موافقة بعضه بعضا ، مما لو احتمل كون مثله عن الخلق لم يمتنع من الخلق من الاختلاف في شيء من ذلك ، دل أنه أنزل من عند علام الغيوب ، ولا قوة إلا بالله
And also that the Quran was revealed in twenty years and more, in separate parts. It did not depart from a single standard of composition and mutual agreement. If it were possible that its like could come from creatures, then creatures would not be prevented from differing in something of that. It indicates that it was sent down from the Knower of the Unseen. And there is no power except with God.
Source pages p. 794

Commentary
This passage is another proof of the Quran's divine origin based on its consistency over a long period of gradual revelation. Maturidi notes that the Quran was revealed over twenty years or more in separate portions, yet it maintains a single standard of composition and internal agreement. If it were a human production, differences and contradictions would inevitably appear. The absence of any inconsistency proves it is from the Knower of the Unseen (علام الغيوب).

Key Terms
التفاريق
النظم
موافقة
علام الغيوب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Quran's consistency is only about its teachings and themes, not its linguistic style.
Correction: Maturidi explicitly uses 'وزن واحد من النظم' (a single standard of composition) to show the consistency includes the very literary structure and wording.

Checkpoint
What would have occurred if the Quran were from a human source, according to Maturidi?
A) It would have been revealed all at once.
B) There would have been differences and contradictions.
C) It would have been more eloquent.
D) It would have been shorter.

Key Takeaway
The Quran's flawless consistency over a twenty-year gradual revelation is a strong rational proof that it is from Allah alone.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
If the Quran's flawless composition is a sign that it is from the Knower of the Unseen, how carefully do you actually listen to its words when you recite or hear them? Are you treating the Quran as a mere human book or as the direct speech of Allah that demands your immediate obedience?
?
What would it look like for your faith to have the same kind of unwavering consistency that the Quran displays—unified and coherent despite the many changes and challenges of life? What is one step you can take this week to remove inconsistency from your worship or your character?

The Challenge to Wish for Death: Proof and Refutation
Maturidi presents a proof from the Quranic challenge and refutes an objection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam Maturidi uses the Quranic challenge to the Jews to wish for death as a proof for the Prophet Muhammad's prophethood, and how he refutes an objection against it.

Core Idea
The unfulfilled challenge to wish for death exposes the Jews' dishonesty and confirms the Prophet.

In this passage, Imam Maturidi presents a powerful argument from the Quranic verse that challenges the Jews to wish for death if they truly are God's chosen people. The fact that they never accepted the challenge, despite it being easy, serves as proof of the Prophet's truthfulness. Maturidi also addresses an objector's attempt to weaken the argument, and his refutation strengthens the proof further.

Guided Path
1
Understand the context
Recall that the verse 'Wish for death' (Quran 2:94) is addressed to the Jews. Maturidi uses it as evidence that the Prophet is true.
The Jews claimed exclusive salvation, so the challenge tests their claim.
2
Identify the two aspects of the proof
Notice that Maturidi draws two conclusions: (1) if they wished, they would die; (2) they never actually wish for it, even though it is easy. This shows their claim is false.
3
Examine the objection and its refutation
Read al-Warraq's two objections and Maturidi's answers carefully. The first objection is about inner intention; the second is about prior knowledge from earlier prophets.
4
Reflect on the strength of the proof
Consider why Maturidi's refutation is effective. The public nature of the Mubahala and the Jews' silence under challenge confirm the argument.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واحتج فى إثبات رسالة محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم مع ما بينا بقوله لليهود : فَتَمَنَّوُا الْمَوْتَ ، بوجهين : أحدهما الوعد بأنهم لو تمنوا الموت لماتوا ، والثانى أنهم لا يتمنون أبدا ، ولا شيء أيسر عليهم من تمنى ذلك ، وبمباهلة النصارى والإخبار بوقوع اللعن ، ثبت أنه معلوم النعت في كتبهم . فأدخل الوراق أنهم لو تمنوا باللسان لقيل إنما أريد به القلب ، والثانى أنهم قد آمنوا بموسى وعيسى ، وقد أخبراهم بذلك كما يخبر المنجمة . فجواب الأول أن المباهلة لا تحتمل ذلك ، وأيضا إنهم أهل بصر ، إذا لو ردوا لقابلوا بأنهم فعلوا ذلك أيضا بقلوبهم والحرف الثانى لو كان كذلك ما امتنعوا عن مقابلته عند قوله : لَتَدْخُلُنَّ
And he argued for establishing the message of Muhammad, peace be upon him, along with what we have explained, by His saying to the Jews: 'Wish for death' with two aspects: one is the promise that if they wished for death they would die, and the second is that they would never wish for it, and nothing is easier for them than wishing for that. And by the Mubahala with the Christians and the informing of the occurrence of the curse, it is established that he is known by description in their books. Then al-Warraq objected that if they wished by tongue, it could be said that only by heart was intended, and second that they had believed in Moses and Jesus, and they had informed them of that just as astrologers inform. The answer to the first is that the Mubahala does not admit that, and also they are people of insight, for if they had rejected, they would have countered that they did that also by their hearts. As for the second point, if it were so, they would not have refrained from countering him at His saying: 'You will certainly enter...'
Source pages p. 794

Commentary
This passage presents a proof from the Quranic challenge to the Jews to wish for death (Quran 2:94) and includes a refutation of an objection. Maturidi argues that the verse implies two things: a promise of death if they wished, and the fact that they never wish for it (despite it being easy). Combined with the Mubahala and the prediction of the curse, this establishes that the Prophet is described in their scriptures. An objector (al-Warraq) raises two points: first, that the wish might be only in the heart, not the tongue; second, that the Jews already believed in Moses and Jesus who informed them, so it is like astrologers' predictions. Maturidi answers that the Mubahala (which was an actual verbal challenge) cannot be reduced to inner intention, and the Jews would have refuted the Prophet if they could have. The second point is refuted by the fact that the Jews did not respond to his challenge.

Key Terms

المباهلة
الوراق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The proof from the challenge is weak because the wish could be internal or the Jews already knew from earlier prophets.
Correction: Maturidi argues that the Mubahala requires public action, and the Jews' silence under direct challenge invalidates their prior knowledge claim.

Checkpoint
What is the first aspect of the proof from the verse 'Wish for death'?
A) The Jews actually wished for death.
B) The promise that if they wished for death they would die.
C) The Jews feared death.
D) The Prophet wished for death.

Key Takeaway
The Quranic challenge to the Jews to wish for death, combined with their refusal, serves as a decisive proof of the Prophet Muhammad's prophethood, supported by the unfulfilled Mubahala and the Jews' inability to counter.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Jews were unwilling to wish for death even though it would have been easy for them. When you claim something about your faith, are you willing to face the ultimate test of that claim? What would it mean for you to 'wish for death' in a moment of spiritual honesty?
?
Maturidi refutes the objection that the Jews might have wished in their hearts. Examine your own heart: is there a gap between what you profess with your tongue and what you truly desire in private? How does this lesson force you to confront the sincerity of your own beliefs?
?
The Jews had prior knowledge but still did not respond to the challenge. Have you ever avoided a situation that would expose the gap between what you know and what you practice? Are you willing to submit your life to the same test that exposes hypocrisy?

The Qur'an's Inimitability in an Age of Ignorance
Maturidi argues that the Qur'an's inimitability is proven by the inability of all scholars to produce its like in that age of polytheism.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's argument that the Qur'an's miraculous nature is proven by the inability of all scholars to produce its like in the era of polytheism.

Core Idea
The Qur'an's inimitability is demonstrated by its emergence in an age of polytheism.

Maturidi presents a unique angle on the Qur'an's inimitability: it was revealed in an age steeped in polytheism, yet even the combined efforts of all monotheists and scholars could not replicate its proofs. This lesson explores how this historical context strengthens the case for the Qur'an's divine origin.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the emphasis on the historical context of polytheism.
2
Identify the key claim
Maturidi argues that the Qur'an is so profound that even all monotheists and scholars from past and future cannot reach a tenth of its proofs. Find this statement in the text.
3
Understand the context
The Prophet was sent in an era where tawheed was unknown and people worshipped idols. Why does Maturidi highlight this? Consider how the context amplifies the miracle.
This connects to the core idea.
4
Reflect on the implications
Think about what this argument says about the Qur'an's origin. If no human can match even a fraction, it must be from God. How does this fit with other proofs of prophethood?
This reinforces the learning objective.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والأصل في هذا أن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم بعث في عصر لم يعرف فيه التوحيد بل كان عباد الأوثان والأصنام والنيران، فجمع ما أنزل عليه القرآن هو من أنجح ما لو اجتمع موحد والعالم من مضى منهم ومن يكون أبدا على إظهار أدلته ما احتملت بلوغ عشرها، فضلا عن الإحاطة في ذلك الزمان الذي لا يقدر على موجد واحد، ولا قوة إلا بالله.
The origin of this is that the Messenger of God, may God bless him and grant him peace, was sent in an age in which tawheed was not known; rather they were worshippers of idols, statues, and fires. So what was revealed to him, the Qur'an, is among the most successful [proofs]—that if a monotheist and the world, from those who have passed and those who will ever be, gathered to manifest its proofs, they would not be capable of reaching a tenth of it, let alone encompassing it, in that time which cannot [produce] a single existent. And there is no power except through God.
Source pages p. 794

Commentary
This passage presents a proof for the miraculous nature of the Qur'an. Maturidi begins by establishing the context: the Prophet was sent in an era dominated by idolatry and polytheism, where tawheed was unknown. The Qur'an, revealed under these circumstances, is so extraordinary that even if all monotheists and scholars of the past and future collaborated to produce its arguments, they could not achieve even a fraction of it. The phrase 'cannot [produce] a single existent' highlights the spiritual barrenness of that age. This argument uses the principle of impossibility (i'jaz) to conclude that the Qur'an must be from God.

Key Terms
التوحيد
القرآن
الإعجاز

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the argument assumes the absence of literate or capable people in that era.
Correction: Actually, Maturidi emphasizes the complete transformation from polytheism to a sophisticated scripture, highlighting the divine origin rather than human capability.

Checkpoint

A) They could easily produce similar proofs given enough time.
B) They could not reach even a tenth of its proofs.
C) They could surpass the Qur'an in eloquence.
D) They could produce a similar work if they collaborated.

Key Takeaway
Maturidi uses the historical context of polytheism to argue that the Qur'an's inimitability is so profound that no human effort could match even a fraction of its proofs, confirming its divine origin.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you had lived in that age of polytheism, what would have convinced you of the truth? But now that you possess the Qur'an, do you let it truly transform your heart away from the modern idols of status, wealth, and self?
?
Maturidi argues that all scholars combined cannot produce a tenth of the Qur'an's proofs. Do you treat the Qur'an as your ultimate authority, or do you secretly seek validation from worldly philosophies and human opinions?
?
That age was spiritually barren. In what specific ways does your own heart resemble that desert, and what would it take for you to let the Qur'an's proofs replace your attachments to false gods?

The Argument from Internal Consistency
Maturidi uses the Qur'an's consistent style and lack of contradiction despite piecemeal revelation over 20 years as proof of divine origin.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Qur'an's internal consistency despite piecemeal revelation over 20 years serves as a proof for its divine origin.

Core Idea
Consistency over time points to a timeless Author.

Imam Maturidi presents a second argument for the Qur'an's divine origin: its remarkable consistency. Despite being revealed in installments over more than twenty years, the Qur'an maintains a unified style and avoids internal contradiction. This passage invites us to reflect on why such consistency would be impossible from human authors and what it reveals about the source of the Qur'an.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice that the passage is a single conditional argument.
2
Identify the key observations
Maturidi makes two observations: the Qur'an was revealed piecemeal over 20+ years, yet it came out on a single pattern of composition (nazm) and mutual consistency.
These two are the basis of the proof.
3
Understand the conditional
The logic is: If creatures had produced such a text, they would inevitably differ in some way. Since the Qur'an shows no discrepancy, it cannot be from creatures.
This is an argument from impossibility.
4
Draw the conclusion
The only remaining possibility is that the Qur'an is from the Knower of the Unseen (Allam al-Ghuyub), who has complete knowledge and is free from error.
5
Reflect on the scope
Consider that the consistency is not just in style but also in meaning—theological and legal rulings remain coherent despite gradual revelation.
This strengthens the argument.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأيضا أن القرآن أنزل في عشرين سنة فصاعدا بالتفاريق، ما خرج إلا على وزن واحد من النظم، وعلى موافقة بعضه بعضا، مما لو احتمل كون مثله عن الخلق لم يمتنع من الخلق من الاختلاف في شيء من ذلك، دل أنه أنزل من عند علام الغيوب، ولا قوة إلا بالله.
And also that the Qur'an was revealed over twenty years and more in installments; it did not come out except upon a single pattern of composition, and upon mutual consistency. For if it were possible that its like came from creatures, then creatures would not refrain from discrepancy in any of that. This indicates that it was sent down from the Knower of the Unseen. And there is no power except through God.
Source pages p. 794

Commentary
This passage presents a second proof for the Qur'an's divine origin: its internal consistency despite being revealed piecemeal over more than twenty years. Maturidi notes that the Qur'an maintains a single, unified style (nazm) and that its parts agree with each other. The argument is that if human beings had produced it, they would inevitably have introduced contradictions or discrepancies over such a long period. The lack of any such inconsistency proves that the Qur'an must be from the All-Knowing (Allam al-Ghuyub), who is free from error.

Key Terms
التفاريق
النظم
علام الغيوب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The argument from consistency only concerns the literary style of the Qur'an.
Correction: Maturidi's argument includes both the single pattern of composition (style) and mutual consistency in meaning, covering theological and legal content as well.

Checkpoint

A) That it was composed by multiple authors.
B) That it was sent down from the Knower of the Unseen.
C) That it can be imitated over time.
D) That it was revealed in stages for gradual implementation.

Key Takeaway
The Qur'an's consistency over 20 years of piecemeal revelation is a sign that its author is the All-Knowing and free from error.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have just seen that the Qur'an's perfect consistency over 20+ years is a sign of its divine origin. But are you consistent in your own relationship with the Qur'an? Do you approach it with the same reverence and urgency as a book from the Knower of the Unseen, or do you treat it like a human work that can be selectively followed? What would need to change today for your heart to align with its Author's consistency?
?
Consider this: if the Qur'an is truly from the All-Knowing, then every command and prohibition is perfectly wise and free of error. Is there any area of your life where you resist or neglect a teaching of the Qur'an because it seems difficult or outdated? Will you, right now, identify one such area and commit to seeking the wisdom behind it, trusting the consistent Author who never contradicts Himself?
